About 2000 people assembled in Eln
tracht Hall, on Twelfth street, last night
to witness the public installation of the
recently elected officers of the local
lodges of ths Order of Hermann's Sons.
The hall was tastefully decorated with
festoons of the German colors, black, red
and cold, and over the stage was a dis
play of large American flags. On ont- side
was thÂ« Stars and Stripes and on tho
other the flag of Germany. The main
floor of- the hall was fitted up as a lodge
room, and after the ofncers-elcct hud
marched Into the hall and were seated In
places assigned to them, the grand offi
cers and ex-grand presidents were an
nounced and admitted. These were Grand
President C. Hahn, Vice President A.
Hagedon, Grand Secretary E. G. Brugge,
Grand Treasurer F. Mlchelsen, Grand
Guide F. W. Reich, and ex-Grand Pres
idents L. Scharenberg, C. Trautner, W.
Rust, Oscar Hocks and D. Voght, the last
named being escorted to seats on the plat
form, while the' others took their re
spective positions at the lodgoroom sta
tions. After the formal opening of the
lodge the several elected officers were
Installed in an Impressive manner by the
grand president, after which the appoint
ed officers were installed by the grand
vice president. During intermissions in
the ceremony the Hermann's Sons* Glee
Club rendered several German vocal se
lections.
After the Installation the grand presi
dent delivered a short address in Ger
man, in which he reviewed the condition
of the order in this State, and announced
that at this time it is In a very prospÂ«r
ous condition, numbering a little more
than 2500, with funds in the different
lodges for the payment of sick and
funeral benefits amounting in the aggre
gate to $90,000. He also stated that during
the last nix months the Increase in mem
bership had been 165 and In finance a lit
tle in excess of $4000. After the proclama
tion of installation the lodgeroom was
dismantled, and there was a grand march,
led by John Hermann, ex-presldÂ«nt of
Eureka Lodge, and wife, after which
there was a long programme of dances,
under the floor directorship of F. W.
Maas, assisted by John Mauer, II. Voight
land, Paul Kaldmann, Emil Lampe and
E. Handmann, tho committee of arrange
ments.

HERMANN'S SONS'
NEW OFFICIALS
NOTED PEOPLE
ON THE SIBERIA
ESbry Savage Landor,
the Famous Traveler,
a Passenger.
Among the passengers who arrived yes
terday on the liner Siberia were several
people of world-wide note. Probably the
best known was A. Henry Savage Landor,
the famous traveler and well known
writer. Landor is on his way" back to
England from the Philippines, where he
has for the last two years been gather
ing material for a book which the Har
pers have engaged him to write. During
his stay in the islands Landor \islted
many of the least heard of places, and
comes away with a high opinion of Uncle
Sam's new possessions. He was with
Captain Pershlng during that officer's
campaign- against the Moros, and speaks
in high terms of the American soldier.
The story of Landor"s journey to Thibet
is well known, and although now In good
health, the little traveler still bears traces
of the two year's illness that followed his
trying experience. Since then, however,
he has journeyed across Asia, and when,
he finishes the work upon which he is now
engaged he will cast about for new worlds
to conquer with his pen and battery of
cameras.
Another illustrious passenger was his
Excellency Major General Sir William
Gascoljme, K. C. M. G., who for the last
five years has been In command of the
British fortes at Hongkong. He has also,
during the absence of Governor Blake, as
sumed that official's duties in the British
province. The general is accompanied by
Lady Gascolgne, with whom he will make
a tour of Southern California before re
suming his journey to England.
John K. Kalanlanaole, better known as
Prince Cupid, Delegate to Congress from
Hawaii, came up on the Siberia. He was
accompanied by the Princess, who accom
panies him on his way to take up his resi
dence in Washington, D. C.
Ington has served two terms in his
present position, and no scandal
has attached to his office."
